# Text Elements
System theory ^Un80X2ih

Regulating systems
Making sure that a system shows desired behavior despite
disturbances. ^xFqwgGCO

System
A concrete unity consisting of elements and relations between these elements
and showing a particular behaviour. Effect is described by variables and values ^hmUb0oIB

Example:
Plank sawing department

elements -> human resources, technology
behaviours -> sowing planks
Effect -> nicely sawn plank
Variables -> quantitiy, quality etc
Regualation -> it is showing desired behaviour if it is sowing 100 
               or more panks per week
Disturbance -> a causer for undisired behaviour
 ^h0Y5DLsW

Recipe for regulation
1. Define a system
    -> concrete: The thing that you describe that shows a certain behaviour
    -> abstract: the set of variables chosen to observe a behavior
2. Determine desired behaviour
3. Identify distrubances.
    -> formulate and perform regulatory actions
 ^J9hImsAE

Complexity of a system
measured in
    -> variety: the number of different states a system can have
    -> state: set of values of the variables of the system at a particular moment in time
 ^FEFwrryy

Concrete sytems vs abstract sytems

In system theory one uses variables in order to describe certian features
of conrete systems at a specific moment in time
example human -> eye color, hair color

The concrete sytem = some real entity that you are describing.
abstract sytem = the set of variables you use to describe the system
Here the state is the values of those variables at some point in time.

Behaviour is described in terms of a sequence of states.


In cybernetics a description of behavior in terms of a sequence of states
is called a transformation ^FILqZnG1

Moment 1 ^pmZAyaR1

Moment 2 ^wnVWssb3

Hiar color ^01y6lS8R

Wrinkels ^d14xVZaW

Brown ^5byIIPSe

gray ^muJ5xdkF

12 ^sISX57x1

327 ^z6xtZQ27

State 1 ^FHcMx2tg

Desired behaviour
Desired behaviour can be described by selecting a norm
value(NV) or region of norm values for the variables of 
the abstract system.

The behaviour is desired if the values of the variables are
within the upper norm-limits.
 ^66cpCx7f

Behaviour ^2dT3QeEs

Input influencing behaviour
The behaviour of concrete systems, which is 
described in terms of the sequance of values of the 
essential variables, is susceptible to
two types of influences
    1. Regulatory actions (positve effect on EV)
    2. Disturbances (negative effect on EV) ^eGCfa0xS

Regulation of concrete systems

For regulation of concrete systems it is important 
to note that 
    1. Essential variables are used to describe behaviour
    2. Parameters are used to model 2 types of influencing factorys
        ->Disturbances and regulatory actions
Regulation can be regarded as making sure that
regulatory parameters are set in such a way  
that the influence of disturbing parameters are
reduced
 ^rO0ugEay

Disturbance
Is an event or state that can cause an essential
variable to move outside its norm value. 
It is causing undesired behaviour ^CAzU8k4Y

Regulatory table ^uZhM2J1D

Distrubance 1 ^VRL28Gyl

Distrubance 2 ^vJWi8Ryb

Distrubance 3 ^RioZMq0S

Regulatory
Action 1 ^Us7y0B34

Regulatory
Action 2 ^qjk0ymxD

Ev 1 ^AbZKdrrq

Ev 1 ^gaTbXUrN

Ev 2 ^uoaez2Oi

Ev 2 ^J5vZMEOT

Ev 3 ^zD3Fe7KA

Ev 3 ^Pd4Bxj2K

This table shows how the values of the essential variables
depend on the values of parameters (D and RA). ^05kWBlnx

Types of regulation
1. Operational regulation
2. Regulation by design
3. Regulation by control ^peNREUuo

Operational regulation
We need to assume that
    1. Disturbances are fixed
    2. Regulatory potential is fixed
    3. The concrete system(infrastructure) does not chagne
    4. The goals are fixed(norm values and Essential variables)

Operational regulations means applying regulatory actions(as given by the concrete system)
in the face of disturbances given the above assumptions. ^SjFBx5ch

Effective vs Efficient operational regulation

Effective -> For every disturbance there is a regulatory action
             that makes sure that the desired values of EV can
             be reached
Efficient ->  If you can be effective with as few regulatory actions
             as possible ^mO2f7e8N

Passive vs active
Passive -> Regulatory action is not selected by a regulator given some
           some disturbance, it is built in the system and works automatically
active  -> A regulator has to select a particular regulatory action for a 
           particular disturbance. A choice BETWEEN regulatory actions has 
           to be made
 ^Oy0prMWE

Error vs cause controlled active regulation
Error-controlled -> The regulatory reacts to damage 
                    and the goals is recovering from damage
                    The distrubance already has an effect
                    on the EV"s
Cause-controlled -> Here the regulator reacts to a threat.
                    The goals is to prevent the damage to the
                    EV's ^IgrVGV9q

Given the above figure we can see that
    1. An infrastructure enables carrying out of processes
    2. An infrastructure has a certain OR potential
    3. An infrastructure is susceptible to certain disturbances
       from either the environment or the infrastructure itself
       can be a disturbance (HR has wrong skills) ^bQKVukOZ

We can deal with these disturbances in 2 ways (excluding OR)
    1. Attenuation
    2. Amplification ^P7MLHmhJ

Attenuation
Decrease the probability of the occurrence of a disturbance
P(D) = 0 ideally. ^DBstWFPG

3 ways of attenuation
1. elimination
    -> Remove Disturbance from the environment.
        e.g. arrest all who make virusses
2. Neutralization
    -> Change the infrastructure or relation with
       environment in such a way that some disturbance
       is is not longer a Disturbance for the system
       Although the disturbance still exists
3. Change infrastructure
    -> change the infrastructure in such a way
        that it itself is no longer a disturbance
        (e.g. Educate workers) ^YyykhCMa

Amplification means changing the infrastructure
by adding more Operational regulatory actions
For example buying an antivirus and installing it.
The moment this application is operational it acts 
as operational regulation ^KeW4nkKn

Regulations by control means that
changing your goals (EV's and NV's)
it is also possible to deal with 
disturbances ^EDBPK7RY

Self Regulation
A self regulating system is a system that
shows a particular behaviour and can carry
out one or more of the activities
Regulation by control, regulation by design
or operational regulation. ^QsuyROIv

Social Systems ^4dDHWIDR

What does it mean for that organizations are social?
Niklus Luhman: "Organizations are autopoietic systems with
'decisions' as elements and with 'decision premisis' as structure  ^ZBFy7ZSj

Autopoietic systems

Autopoietic systems are 'self-producing' systems.
That is, an autopoietic system consists out of elements
that interact with each other and by means of their
interaction they product elements the system consist of.
->
As the interacting elements of an autopoietic system produce 
elements of the system, they also produce the system as a whole, 
that is, by means of their interactions these elements secure the
survival of the system in its environment.

 ^sUXCwYC3

3 Criteria for autopoeitic system
    1. A system must be able to "shrink" itself
    2. A system must be able to "persist" itself
    3. A system must be able to enlarge itself ^lbGXMoyh

Social autopoeitic systems ^jIidixaV

what are the elements of social systems?

Luhman: Elements of a social system is communication.
Communication is a unity of 3 aspects
    1. Information -> What is being communicated
    2. Utterance -> the decision that something is being
                     communicated and HOW something is 
                     being communicated
    3. Understanding -> Understanding that an utterance was selected
                         to communicate information and understanding
                        the information itself 
Information and Utterance is done by initiator and understanding is done
by the respondent.

Communication is produced by 2 participants who themselves are NOT elements
of the social system. ^dB1pcPUr

What is the social system itself?
A social system is a while of meaningfully connected communications.
In a social system a communication leads to a follow-up communication.
The social  system refers to this sequence of communications that
meaningfully blend together. ^P4bvjxAT

What is the structure of a social system?
Or What is it that makes this communication meaningful?
Luhman: It is the strucure of a social system that is used to 
determine meaningfulness. 
He defines the structure of a social system as the set of 
'expectations of expectations' that participants in communication
have of eachother. ^q3GIHmU1

Expectations of expectations
If A and B are participants in communication tha

A expects that B expects certain behaviour/reactions of A
B expects that A expects certain behaviour/reactions of B

This will influence the behaviour of both A and B. ^rMnpyl7h

What is a social system as an autopoietic system?
in an autopoietic system, the elements of the system ‘produce’ new elements
In a social system communication will lead to more communication. ^4kE58sZy

Organisations as autopoietic social systems ^otp7xZWr

What are the elements of organizations as social systems?

Decisions.
A decision is a communication in which the information refers
to the selection of a particular option out of a set of options.

It refers to:
    1. The option
    2. the fact that this option is selected. ^3bYwg6NG

What is the organisation as a social system?

An organisation is a 'whole of meaningfully connected' decisions.
 ^TOqIiSNq

What is the structure of an organisation
as a social system?

structure helps to 
    1. Determine that a communication can be
      regarded as a decision.
    2. And to determine which decisions are allowed
       as decisions of a particular organisation.
 
 ^As0MjK3j

Example:
Decisions premisis ->
personnel: this premise determines who in the organisation
          is allowed to participate in decision making ^Wt3ZuvBb

What is an organisation as an autopoietic social system?
Decisions will lead to more decisions
    1. Decision lead to follow up decisions -> if this does
      not happen the organisation will no longer exist
    2. Decisions are about goals, infrastructure and OR.
       the moment something is decided this is the basis
       for communication/decisions
    3. Based on 2, decisions are related to
       the experiment
    4. Decision premise(structure) can change ^Rvt98fZN

Viability ^CZSefaS8

Being able to maintain a separate existance ^S5dflgFQ

Difficult to remain viable
Beer -> difficult because of complexity.
If organisations cannot deal with complexity
they can't survive ^Jr5i8rbK

Complexity paradox

1.  The complexity of the environment is much larger than that of
   an organisation
2. The complexity of the organization is much larger than that of
   of it's management
3. Systems need complexity to deal with complexity
4. Given the mismatch in complexity, management can't deal with
   the complexity of organisations and organisations can't deal
   with the complexity of the environment.
5. BUT -> organisations exist ^8iUEbYWd

How to remain viable

Beer:
Organisations only have to deal with RELEVANT environmental complexity
Relevance is determined by setting goals

Thus we have to deal with vareity
3 ways: 
    1. attenuate variety -> take away disturbances
    2. amplify -> regulatory potential
    3. recursion ^Wq75L71p

Recursion ^M6lsP6t6

within a concrete system another concrete system can be found
with the same relevant features as the overarching concrete system ^6Xg7p5F6

Concrete system A
Has features 1,2,3,4 ^JKgDIqYe

Concrete system B;
also has features
1,2,3,4 ^mvTgdlQD

Also called a subsystem of A ^XkCi9DYF

Beer:
If in organisations subsystems have the capacity to
    1. Set goals
    2. Attenuate/amplify
    3. Operational regulation

these subsystems become autonomous 
    -> If they can deal with their own disturbances
       they higher level system does not have to deal with them ^g1kIbmGe

VSM ^30uhuMXq

5 functions that should be 
realized in organisations so as to make sure
they remain viable ^DbsGhesi

Function 1
The collection or primary activities
 ^fJz55g3f

Function 2
Coordination
goal: deal with interferences that
can occur between primary activities ^5b8UM0w0

These interferences happen because of
    1. shared resources
    2. shared goals ^olA39QVJ

function 3
control
3 tasks:
    1. Translating strategy into targers 
      for primary activities
    2. Monitoring targets set for function 1
    3. Setting goals for and monitoring the 
       activities of function 2.
    4. Evaluate plans for innovation(function 4) ^SjijngxS

Function 4:
Intelligence. This function should scan the 
environment and translate trends/developments
into plans for innovation ^oL3EYloL

Function 5:
Policy
regulate strategic discussion ^VwHJGih9

How they work ^Wex0Y74e

Function 3 and 4 engage is strategic discussion

If F4(intelligence) proposes new plans for innovation
and the organisation is leaning towards not doing anything
conservatism is winning -> F3 is dominant
otherwise innovatism is winning -> F4 is dominant  ^uT3oJ11h

VSM is a recusrive model -> if function 1 exists
all other functions will also exist.

VSM is a functional model. It does not specify
what the infrastructure should look like ^N5wBH4T9

VSM formulates functional design principles ^stE9v5ol

Viable system model ^by5Yoa75

Function 1.
Primary process ^PLspHAc9

Function 2
Deal with
interferences ^yjxt1wcl

Environment ^zuJZVXNp

Function 3 ^e5nBHTa9

Function 4 ^6IdvbEMQ

Research ^8WNv9Y5U

Monitors ^GqrnOXrn
